Here is a revised version of Output (b) that addresses the issues I mentioned in my evaluation:  Prosopagnosia, also known as face blindness, is a condition where individuals cannot recognize faces, including those of their loved ones. People with this condition can see individual facial features such as eyes, nose, and mouth, but cannot process them as a whole, making it difficult to recognize gestures or emotions. This can lead to social embarrassment and challenges in daily life, as affected individuals may not recognize friends, family members, or colleagues in various situations. The symptoms of prosopagnosia include difficulty recognizing faces, even those of people they know well, and difficulty recognizing gestures or emotions. There are two main forms of prosopagnosia: developmental and acquired. Developmental affects around 2% of the population and acquired is much rarer, caused by damage to the back of the brain on the right-hand side
